CERTIFICATION OF MEDICAL RECORDS
To the best of myknowledge, the copied documents, records and other items enclosed are true and correct copies of all
original records identified and described in the subpoena duces tecum, patient authorization, or court order made by or at
the direction of the custodian of records. The original records were prepared in the ordinary course of the facility's
regularly conducted business at or near the time of the act, candition, or event by persons with knowledge of the facts
recorded, and the records have been maintained in the ardinary course of the facility’s regularly conducted business
according to all confidentiality and security requirements of law. This certification is given by the custodian of records
instead of the custodian’s personal appearance.
We are not aware of any omissions; however, due to the timing of this request it is possible that a portion of the medical
record may be incomplete and/or preliminary atthis time.
The recipient of these records agrees to maintain their confidentiality and permit further disclosure only as authorized by
law.

Ciox Validation Checklist -—ROI Standard Requests
Please use the as a checklist when validating your general ROI requests and authorizations.
Actions
Patient information, including two identifiers (example: full name, date of birth or social security
number).
Name of a provider authorized to release the information.
Name of individual or provider authorized to receive the information.
Specific information to be disclosed/released and re-disclosed /re-released
(information contained in the chart may contain records from another facility and were
used in the course of treatment of the patient; they may be re-released).
Sensitive information release/non-release. The patient must expressly authorize the release of
AIDS/HIV, Drug/Alcohol abuse treatment, mental health, GINA, STDs, etc.
Disclosure / re-disclosure statement. A statement that explains that the patient's health
information may no longer be protected by federal privacy regulations once ithas been
released by the medical facility to the authorized recipient.
Right to revoke statement - The patient has the right to revoke the authorization at a later
time provided it has not been acted upon. It must include how to revoke.
Conditions statement —A statement about the ability or inability of the CE to condition
treatment, payment, enrollment or eligibility of benefits on whether the individual signs the
authorization. | understand that the medical provider to whom this authorization is
furnished may not condition its treatment of me on whether or not | sign the authorization.
HCA/Ciox EXCEPTION: Authorizations sent by attorneys and any others who cannot
withhold medical treatment are not required to contain the ‘conditioning’ statement.
Purpose of the disclosure statement —Why the patient wants the records to be released.
Authorization expiration: Specific date, event or condition for which consent will expire
unless revoked earlier.
Signature of patient or legal Representative (the signature of the patient must be verified
by checking the Consent for Treatment/Condition of Admissions form or driver's license). LINISIN
Date authorization was signed. Check to verify that the authorization is not expired
based expiration information above.

Conditions of Admission and Consent for Outpatient Care
MARSHALL, DEBBIE 
In this document, "Patient" means the person receiving treatment. "Patient Representative" means any person 
acting on behalf of the Patient and signing as the Patient’s representative. Use of the word “I,” “you,” “your” or 
“me” may in context include both the Patient and the Patient Representative. With respect to financial obligations 
“I” or “me” may also, depending on the context, mean financial guarantor “Guarantor”.
"Provider" means the hospital and may include healthcare professionals on the hospital’s staff and/or hospitalbased physicians, which include but are not limited to: Emergency Department Physicians, Pathologists, 
Radiologists, Anesthesiologists, Hospitalists, certain other licensed independent practitioners and any authorized 
agents, contractors, affiliates, successors or assignees acting on their behalf.
1. Legal Relationship between Hospital and Physicians and Advanced Practice Professionals. I understand 
and acknowledge that the physicians and advanced practice professionals providing services to me in the hospital 
are independent contractors and not agents or employees of the hospital. "Advanced Practice Professionals"
include, but are not limited to, my treating physicians/ surgeons, radiologists, pathologists, cardiologists, 
emergency physicians, anesthesiologists, contract physicians, hospital-based physicians, physician assistants, 
registered nurses, advanced practice registered nurses, certified nurse midwives, certified registered nurse 
anesthetists, clinical psychologists, clinical nurse specialists, doctors of nursing practice, radiology assistants, and 
anesthesiology assistants. Independent physicians and Advanced Practice Professionals are responsible for their 
own actions and the hospital shall not be liable for the acts or omissions of any such independent physicians and/
or Advanced Practice Professionals.
2. Consent to Treatment. I consent to the procedures that may be performed during this hospitalization or during 
an outpatient episode of care, including, but not limited to, emergency treatment or services, and which may 
include laboratory procedures, x-ray examination, diagnostic procedures, medical, nursing or surgical treatment 
or procedures, anesthesia, or hospital services rendered as ordered by the Provider. I consent to allowing residents 
and other individuals enrolled in a healthcare professional education program as part of their training in health 
care education to participate in the delivery of my medical care and treatment or be observers while I receive 
medical care and treatment at the Hospital, and that they will be supervised by instructors and/or hospital staff. I 
further consent to the hospital conducting blood-borne infectious disease testing, including but not limited to, 
testing for hepatitis, Acquired Immune Deficiency Syndrome (“AIDS”), and Human Immunodeficiency Virus 
(“HIV”), if a Provider orders such tests or if ordered by protocol. I understand that the potential side effects and 
complications of this testing are generally minor and are comparable to the routine collection of blood specimens, 
including discomfort from the needle stick and/or slight burning, bleeding or soreness at the puncture site. The 
results of this test will become part of my confidential medical record.
3. Consent to Treatment Using Telemedicine. I consent to treatment involving the use of electronic 
communications ("Telemedicine") to enable health care providers at different locations to share my individual 
patient medical information for diagnosis, therapy, follow-up, and/or education purposes. I consent to forwarding 
my information to a third party as needed to receive Telemedicine services, and I understand that existing 
confidentiality protections apply. I acknowledge that while Telemedicine can be used to provide improved access 
to care, as with any medical procedure, there are potential risks and no results can be guaranteed or assured.
These risks include, but are not limited to: technical problems with the information transmission or equipment

MARSHALL, DEBBIE 
failures that could result in lost information or delays in treatment. I understand that I have a right to withhold or 
withdraw my consent to the use of Telemedicine in the course of my care at any time, without affecting my right 
to future treatment and without risking the loss or withdrawal of any program benefit to which I would otherwise 
be entitled.
4. Use of Biological Samples. During your care at the facility, biological samples (such as blood and tissue 
samples) might be collected from you for purposes of your care. Sometimes, after your visit there might be 
excess or leftover biological samples no longer needed for your care. These samples are usually discarded. 
However, sometimes these samples might be used for research within our hospitals and occasionally made 
available to researchers at external groups such as universities, private companies, advocacy groups, and 
government agencies. The research can help answer questions about the causes of diseases, how to prevent them, 
or even how to treat them. Please note that for this kind of research, (i) there might be no practical way to inform 
you about the details or results of the research (even if it involves genetic research), (ii) generally, no results on 
tests performed on your samples during the research can be returned to you or entered into your health record, 
(iii) it is not likely that you will directly benefit from the research, and (iv) there are no plans to compensate or 
recognize you for use of your samples or any discoveries made during the research. When these samples are used 
in this manner, your privacy is safeguarded consistent with applicable federal and state privacy laws.
5. Consent to Medication Not Yet FDA Approved and/or Medication Prepared/Repackaged by Outsourcing
or Compounding Pharmacy. As part of the services provided, you may be treated with a medication that has not 
received FDA approval. You may also receive a medication that has been prepared or repackaged by an 
outsourcing facility or compounding pharmacy. Certain medications for which there are no alternatives or which 
your physician recommends may be necessary for potentially life-saving treatment.
6. Consent to Product Patient Assistance Programs Limited Power of Attorney (“LPOA"). The Provider 
may be able to get free replacement or reimbursement for the cost of your drugs or medical products from the 
companies that make them through a patient assistance program sponsored by the companies that make your 
drugs or medical products and through charity foundations. If the hospital obtains replacement or reimbursement 
of cost of your drug or medical product from the manufacturer through such programs, the charge for the product 
or drug will be removed from your bill. Patient assistance programs require you to sign an application form in 
order for the hospital to obtain replacement or credits of certain drugs administered or devices implanted to 
qualifying patients. This LPOA allows the Provider and its claims processor to complete and sign your patient 
assistance program applications for you for so long as this program may be available to you.
I hereby appoint hospital and/or its claims processor, my attorney-in-fact for the sole and exclusive purpose of 
signing patient assistance program application forms on my behalf, so that hospital may attempt to obtain 
replacement or credits of certain drugs administered or devices implanted from the companies that make them. I 
understand that the final decision as to my acceptance in a patient assistance program lies with each 
pharmaceutical or medical device company and that submission by hospital provides no guarantee or assurance 
that any application will be approved. I will provide reasonable assistance and additional information and 
documentation as necessary to support each application.

payment enrollment, or eligibility for benefits may not be conditioned upon signing this authorization; and 4) I 
may revoke this authorization at any time by notifying the Provider in writing at 
, however, such revocation will not affect any actions taken prior to facility receiving the revocation.
This LPOA shall be in full force from the date signed and continue for so long as these programs may be 
available to you.

7. Consent to Photographs, and Video, Digital and Audio Recordings. I consent to photographs, video,digital 
or audio recordings, and/or images of me being recorded for patient care, healthcare operations, security purposes 
and/or the hospital’s quality improvement and/or risk management activities. I understand that the facility retains 
the ownership rights to the images and/or recordings. I will be allowed to request access to or copies of the 
images and/or recordings when technologically feasible unless otherwise prohibited by law. I understand that 
these images and/or recordings will be securely stored and protected. Images and/or recordings in which I am 
identified will not be released and/or used outside of the facility without a specific written authorization from me 
or my legal representative unless otherwise required by law.
8. Financial Agreement. In consideration of the services to be rendered to Patient, Patient or Guarantor 
individually promises to pay the Patient’s account at the rates stated in the hospital’s price list (known as the 
"Charge Master" ) effective on the date the charge is processed for the service provided, which rates are hereby 
expressly incorporated by reference as the price term of this agreement to pay the Patient’s account. Some special 
items will be priced separately if there is no price listed on the Charge Master. An estimate of the anticipated 
charges for services to be provided to the Patient is available upon request from the hospital. Estimates may vary 
significantly from the final charges based on a variety of factors, including, but not limited to, the course of 
treatment, intensity of care, physician practices, and the necessity of providing additional goods and services.
The hospital will provide a medical screening examination as required to all Patients who are seeking medical 
services to determine if there is an emergency medical condition without regard to the Patient’s ability to pay. If 
there is an emergency medical condition, the hospital will provide stabilizing treatment within its capacity. 
However, Patient and Guarantor understand that if Patient does not qualify under the hospital’s charity care 
policy or other applicable policy, Patient or Guarantor is not relieved of his/her obligation to pay for these 
services.

MARSHALL, DEBBIE 
If supplies and services are provided to Patient who has coverage through a governmental program or through 
certain private health insurance plans, the hospital may accept a discounted payment for those supplies and 
services. In this event any payment required from the Patient or Guarantor will be determined by the terms of the 
governmental program or private health insurance plan. If the Patient is uninsured and not covered by a 
governmental program, the Patient may be eligible to have his or her account discounted or forgiven under the 
hospital’s uninsured discount or charity care programs in effect at the time of treatment. I understand that I may 
request information about these programs from the hospital. 
I also understand that, as a courtesy to me, the hospital may bill an insurance company offering coverage, but 
may not be obligated to do so. Regardless, I agree that, except where prohibited by law, the financial 
responsibility for the services rendered belongs to me, the Patient or Guarantor. I agree to pay for services that are 
not covered and covered charges not paid in full by insurance coverage including, but not limited to, coinsurance, 
deductibles, non-covered benefits due to policy limits or policy exclusions, or failure to comply with insurance 
plan requirements.
I also understand that an itemized statement of all charges for which the patient or a third-party payor of patient is 
being billed by the hospital for items/services rendered to him/her while a patient of the hospital will be available 
to the patient on a link on each hospital’s website. Each patient who has been discharged from the hospital, or his/
her legal representative will be able to view the itemized or detailed bill through the website link. The itemized or 
detailed bill will be updated each time a bill is created, for example, with any rebills or edits or upon request for 
an itemized or detailed bill. I may obtain a copy of my itemized bill(s) by going to my facility’s website. 
9. Professional services rendered by independent contractors and Advanced Practice Professionals are not 
part of the hospital bill. I understand that physicians and other Advanced Practice Professionals may be called 
upon to provide care or services to me or on my behalf, but that I may not actually see, or be examined by all 
physicians or other Advanced Practice Professionals participating in my care; for example, I may not see 
physicians, including but not limited to, my treating physicians/ surgeons, radiologists, pathologists, 
cardiologists, emergency physicians, anesthesiologists, staff physicians, contract physicians, physician assistants 
and other Advanced Practice Professionals including those providing radiology, pathology, EKG interpretation, 
anesthesiology services or telemedicine. I understand that, in most instances, there will be a separate charge for 
professional services rendered by these providers and that I will receive a bill for these professional services that 
is separate from the bill for hospital services.
10. Third Party Collection. I acknowledge that the Providers may utilize the services of a third party Business
Associate or affiliated entity as an extended business office (“EBO Servicer”) for medical account billing and 
servicing. During the time that the medical account is being serviced by the EBO Servicer, the account shall not 
be considered delinquent, past due or in default. When the EBO Servicer’s efforts to obtain payment have been 
exhausted due to a number of factors (for e.g., Patient or Guarantor’s failure to pay or make a payment 
arrangement after insurance adjustments and payments have been credited, and/or the insurer’s denial of claim(s) 
or benefits is received), the EBO Servicer will send a final notice letter which will include the date that the 
medical account may be returned from the EBO Servicer to the Provider. Upon return to the Provider by the EBO 
Servicer, the Provider may place the account back with the EBO Servicer, or, at the option of the Provider, may 
determine the account to be delinquent, past due and in default.

11. Assignment of Benefits. Patient assigns all of his/her rights and benefits under existing policies of insurance 
providing coverage and payment for any and all expenses incurred as a result of services and treatment rendered

(C) The Glomerular Filtration Rate is a calculated parameter
based on serum Creatinine levels, patient age, and sex. GFR
values less than 60 mL/min/1.73 square meters are indicative of Chronic Kidney Disease. Values less than 15 mL/min/1.73
square meters indicate Kidney failure. The calculation for
GFR is based on the CKD-EPI(2021) calculation. This formula is race indifferent and is the recommended formula for GFR
by the National Kidney Foundation for adults. The GFR will
not calculate if the sex is Unknown or if the patient's age is <18 years. We will continue to report a race factor eGFR
along with this new result until December 31, 2022.

(C) The Glomerular Filtration Rate is a calculated parameter
based on serum Creatinine levels, patient age, and sex. GFR
values less than 60 mL/min/1.73 square meters are indicative
of Chronic Kidney Disease. Values less than 15 mL/min/1.73
square meters indicate Kidney failure. The calculation for
GFR is based on the CKD-EPI(2021) calculation. This formula
is race indifferent and is the recommended formula for GFR
by the National Kidney Foundation for adults. The GFR will
not calculate if the sex is Unknown or if the patient's age
is <18 years. We will continue to report a race factor eGFR
along with this new result until December 31, 2022.
(D) Units of measure: ml/min/1.73 m2
Stages of Kidney Damage according to the National Kidney
Foundation are defined as follows:
Stage 1 Kidney damage with normal kidney function
>= 90 ml/min/1.73 m2
Stage 2 Kidney damage with mildly decreased kidney function
60-89 ml/min/1.73 m2
Stage 3a Kidney damage with mildly to moderately decreased
kidney function 45-59 ml/min/1.73 m2
Stage 3b Kidney damage with moderately to severely decreased
kidney function 30-44 ml/min/1.73 m2
Stage 4 Kidney damage with severely decreased kidney
function 15-29 ml/min/1.73 m2
Stage 5 Kidney failure <15 ml/min/1.73 m2

(I) The Glomerular Filtration Rate is a calculated parameter
based on serum Creatinine levels, patient age, and sex. GFR
values less than 60 mL/min/1.73 square meters are indicative
of Chronic Kidney Disease. Values less than 15 mL/min/1.73
square meters indicate Kidney failure. The calculation for
GFR is based on the CKD-EPI(2021) calculation. This formula
is race indifferent and is the recommended formula for GFR
by the National Kidney Foundation for adults. The GFR will
not calculate if the sex is Unknown or if the patient's age
is <18 years. We will continue to report a race factor eGFR
along with this new result until December 31, 2022.

See page 2 of this notice for more information.

Important Message from Medicare
You can be involved in any decisions about your hospital stay.
You can receive Medicare covered services. This includes medically necessary hospital services and 
services you may need after you are discharged, if ordered by your doctor. You have a right to know
about these services, who will pay for them, and where you can get them.
Your Rights as a Hospital Inpatient:
Your Right to Appeal Your Hospital Discharge:
Form CMS 10065-IM (Exp. [DOB-304])
You can work with the hospital to prepare for your safe discharge and arrange for services you 
may need after you leave the hospital. When you no longer need inpatient hospital care, your 
doctor or the hospital staff will inform you of your planned discharge date.
•
• You can speak with your doctor or other hospital staff if you have concerns about being discharged.
You have the right to an immediate, independent medical review (appeal) of the decision to 
discharge you from the hospital. If you do this, you will not have to pay for the services you 
receive during the appeal (except for charges like copays and deductibles).
If you choose to appeal, the independent reviewer will ask for your opinion. The reviewer also 
will look at your medical records and/or other relevant information. You do not have to prepare 
anything in writing, but you have the right to do so if you wish. 
If you choose to appeal, you and the reviewer will each receive a copy of a detailed explanation 
about why your covered hospital stay should not continue. You will receive this detailed notice 
only after you request an appeal.
If the QIO finds that you are not ready to be discharged from the hospital, Medicare will 
continue to cover your hospital services. 
If the QIO agrees services should no longer be covered after the discharge date, neither 
Medicare nor your Medicare health plan will pay for your hospital stay after noon of the day 
after the QIO notifies you of its decision. If you stop services no later than that time, you will 
avoid financial liability. 
You can report any concerns you have about the quality of care you receive to your QIO at:KEPRO 
1-[PHONE-238] or TTY [PHONE-239]. The QIO is the independent reviewer authorized by 
Medicare to review the decision to discharge you.
•
•
•
•
•
•
• If you do not appeal, you may have to pay for any services you receive after your discharge date.
OMB approval 0938-1019

Urinary
Management
Protocol
(continued)
706105
NDFP
empowers
nursing
to
remove
indwelling
urinary
catheters
(IUC)
as
soon as
theyareno
longer
clinically indicated.
Nurses
can
remove
the
urinary
catheter without
a
specific
order
or
provider approval.
A.
Appropriate indications
for
maintaining
an
indwelling
urinary catheter
include:
1.
Accurate
[&0 and
critically
il]
2.
Acute
retention/obstruction
3.
Assist
in
skin
healing
4.
Gross
hematuria/bladder
irrigation
5.
Palliative
care 6.
Prolonged
immobilization
7.
Peripartum
B.
Assess
need
of
catheter
daily.
If
patient
no
longer meets
indication
criteria
above
foran 1.
indwelling
urinary catheter
and the
patient
doesnot have
a
reason for the
catheter
to
continue,
then the
catheter
will
be
discontinued.
Remove before
12
noon
if
possible.
URINARY CATHETER ALGORITHM
FOR
ACUTE
RETENTION
AND
EARLY
REMOVAL (UCARE)
UCARE
empowers
the
nurse
to
remove
the
indwelling
urinary catheter
(IUC) on day
2 of
acute
urinary retention
and
assist patient
in
using active
voiding
measures
as
listed below.
By
removing
the IUC
after
the
acute time
frame,
the
current
status
can be
better
understood
for
resolution
or
continued
issues
that may need
to be
further
addressed
by
specialties.
While
in
use,
nursing
can
utilize
the
in/out
(straight)
catheter
with
bladder
scan
as
long
as
tolerated
by the
patient.
A.
Post
IUC
removal,
follow
the
Urinary Catheter Algorithm
for
Acute
Retention
and
Early
Removal (UCARE)
1.
Encourage
active
voiding.
If
not
voided
in 4-6
hours,
scan
bladder.
2. If
<
180 mL:
Assess intake,
encourage
active
voiding, reassess
in
4
hours.
a.
If
not
voiding within
2 If
180-500
mL:
Encourage
active
voiding. hours,
scan
bladder.
b.
If
residual
urine
<
180 mL: No
further action, continue
to
monitor.
2.
Residual
urine
>
180 mL
1.
Continue
active
voiding, report
residual
volume
to
primary
team. 3. NO
residual
urine: Repeat algorithm
If
>
500 mL:
Perform in/out
catheter
and
repeat
algorithm
1.
May
perform in/out
catheter
for
a
minimum
of
4
cycles
and
Cc.
continue
as
tolerated
If
voiding
spontaneously:
continue
to
monitor
3.
<End
of
Protocol>

PATIENT: MARSHALL, DEBBIE

LOC: G.ERHOLD DISCH/DEP: 12/04/22
RM: G.ERI1 STATUS: IN
BD: A UNIT NO: G001075275
Protocol: <Rapid Response Protocol Protocol>
*#* Rapid Response Protocol ***
A. Nursing Orders: (All patients)
Insert peripheral IV if No patent IV access
Establish and maintain the patient's airway
Continuous cardiac monitoring place on bedside monitor
Initiate Oxygen Therapy Protocol
* Oxygen Therapy: Only start on Oxygen therapy if SpO2 is less than
than 90%
* Device: Nasal Cannula
* Rate: 1 Liter per minute 2 L/Min
* Initiate 02 Therapy Protocol: Yes No
* Initiate 02 weaning protocol: Yes No
* Titrate to Maintain Sp02: 90-96%
if greater than 51 nasal cannula required change to face mask
starting at 40% Fi02 and Notify provider.
Suction Airway as needed
Notify attending physician of change in patient status and
interventions performed.
Fingerstick blood glucose now
Give 25 milliliters of D50 if blood glucose below 80
Give 50 milliliters of D50 if blood glucose below 60
B. Cardiac Clinical Changes:
Heart Rate less than 40 (symptomatic)
1.) Atropine 1 milligram intravenous push now per ACLS protocol
Heart Rate greater than 180 (symptomatic)
1.) 12 Lead EKG Now
Chest Pain
1.) EKG Now and give to a provider within 10 minutes - may give to ED
provider or in-house provider.
2.) Aspirin 81 milligrams orally x 4 chewed and swallow if no
allergies, active bleeding, warfarin use, or unless taken within
the last 24 hours
3.) Nitroglycerin 0.4 milligrams sublingual, may repeat every 5
minutes x2 doses if systolic BP greater than 90
4.) Troponin stat
5.) Upon identification of ST-Elevation initiate the STEMI process.
Call hospital operator to page out Stemi Alert.
Systolic Blood Pressure less than 90 (symptomatic)
1.) Normal saline 250 milliliters intravenous bolus if no crackles,
rhonchi or complaints of dyspnea; may repeat x 1
C. Respiratory Allergy and Anaphylaxis:
STAT Portable Chest x-ray (obtain if an acute respiratory distress
problem).
Administer nebulized Albuterol 2.5 mg (unless patient is presently on
a nebulizer treatment protocol) in 3 mL saline.
Arterial Blood Gas per Respiratory Therapy if unable to improve
saturation with oxygen therapy and or suspected CO2 retention. If BiPap required, initiate with the following settings, inspiratory
pressure of 12 cm H20, expiratory pressure of 6cm H20, titrating as
indicated
Patient assessment of crackles/rhonchi and patient complaint of
dyspnea
1.) administer furosemide (Lasix) 20 milligrams intravenous now.
2.) Decrease/Discontinue IV fluids
D. Respiratory (Upper Airway): altered level of consciousness, edema of
or the face, lips, tongue or throat, nasal congestion, rhinitis,
sneezing cough, hoarseness or quiet voice, lost ability to speak or
a sensation of tightness in the throat, strider, hypoxia:
1.) Initiate code blue event
2.) Initiate all other interventions, general and specific to the

OneContent: Generated By HCA\EAZ4474 Generated On: [DOB-360] 16:02
rapid response protocol
E. Respiratory (Lower Airway) wheezing:
Cardiovascular: tachycardia, hypotension, chest pain
Skin: urticaria, angioedema, flushing, pruritis
Gastrointestinal: nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, cramping, pain
Neurological: headache, dizziness, sense of impending doom seizures
1.) Establish and maintain patient airway
2.) Place patient in supine position and elevate lower extremities
3.) Remove source of the antigen if possible
F. Systolic Blood Pressure greater than 90mmHg and no Respiratory
compromise:
1.) Diphenhydramine (Benadryl) 25 milligrams intravenous (IM if no IV
access) x 1
2.) Famotidine (Pepcid) 20 milligrams intravenous x 1
3.) Hydrocortisone (Solu-Cortef) 250 milligrams intravenous (IM if no
IV access) x 1 dose
4.) If no improvement, epinephrine 1:1000 0.3 milligrams
intra-muscular lateral thigh every 15 minutes as needed x 3 doses
G. Systolic Blood Pressure less than 90mmHg and/or Respiratory compromise:
1.) Normal saline 250 milliliters intravenous bolus; may repeat as
needed x 3 doses
2.) Epinephrine 1:1000 0.3 milligrams intra-muscular lateral thigh
every 15 minutes as needed x 3 doses
3.) Diphenhydramine (Benadryl) 25 milligrams intravenous (IM if no IV
access) x 1
4.) Famotidine (Pepcid) 20 milligrams intravenous x 1
5.) Hydrocortisone (Solu-Cortef) 250 milligrams intravenous (IM if no
IV access) x 1 dose
6.) If on beta blocker and not responding to epinephrine, give
glucagon hydrochloride (Glucagon) 3 milligrams intravenous (IM if
no IV access)
7.) If having anaphylaxis-associated bronchospasm, respiratory
treatment of most preferred - albuterol aerosol treatment 0.5
milligrams in 3 milliliters normal saline OR least preferred -
albuterol inhaler (MDI) (Proventil) 17 grams 2 puffs every 4 hours
as needed
8.) Transfer to ICU
H. Sepsis:
Administer Normal Saline IV fluid bolus up to 500 milliliters
Complete Metabolic Panel Stat
Complete Blood Count with Differential Stat
Draw Lactate Stat
Blood Cultures x 2. 2 different sites
I. Altered Mental Status suspected Stroke:
Implement Inpatient Code Stroke Protocol
J. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status:
Initiate Oxygen Therapy Protocol
Cardiac Monitor
Finger stick blood sugar and follow hypoglycemic protocol
K. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status post narcotic
administration:
Naloxone (Narcan) 0.2 milligrams IV push now if recent narcotic
administered and any of the following are present:
1.) Decreased level of consciousness
2.) Pinpoint pupils (less than 3 mm)
3.) Respiratory rate less than 8/min
May repeat naloxone (Narcan) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push after 5
minutes to a maximum of 0.4 milligrams total
L. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status post
benzodiazepine administration:
Flumazenil (Romazicon) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push now if recent
Benzodiazepine administered and any of the following are present:
1.) Decreased level of consciousness
2.) Respiratory rate less than 8/min
May repeat flumazenil (Romazicon) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push every
1 minute to a maximum of 1 milligram total.

** Caution: flumazenil (Romazicon) administration is not recommended for
patients receiving chronic benzodiazepine therapy
M. New onset or prolonged seizures:
Lorazepam (Ativan) 1 milligram intravenous push; may repeat x 1 for
witnessed seizure
N. Hypertensive Crisis:
Labetalol intravenous per PRN order
Hydralazine intravenous per PRN order
0. Decrease in Urine Output:
Urine output less than 50 milliliters in 4 hours
1.) Normal saline 250 milliliters intravenous bolus if no crackles,
rhonchi and or complaints of dyspnea; may repeat x 1
2.) Straight Cath patient to measure retention
P. Laboratory Testing:
Labs to be drawn at the discretion of the rapid response team.
1.) BMP (arrhythmias, diuresis, acid-base imbalance)
2.) MG (arrhythmias, known hypokalemia)
3.) CBC (suspected bleeding and/or hypotension)
4.) Blood glucose finger stick (change in level of consciousness)
<End of Protocol>

NURORDNI Pain Medication Preference 20221203-0131 12/03/22 2225 R E TRN CHECHO1
Other Provider : xxWILAD Sig Lvl Provider :
A medication prescribed for a lower pain scale rating than the currently
reported pain rating may be administered based on pt. preference if:
* An order for the alternative medication being requested already exists
in the patient’s medical record.
* Administration of substituted med doesn’t create therapeutic duplication.
* Contact provider for a new order if these conditions are not met.
* Documentation in the medical record must reflect that the less potent med
was administered based on patient request.
* Tt is never acceptable to substitute a medication prescribed for a higher
pain rating based on patient request.

Patient: MARSHALL, DEBBIE MRN: G001075275
<Oxygen Therapy Protocol>
-- Oxygen Therapy Protocol: Adult --
INITIATION:
A. Supplemental oxygen will occur after verification of a provider’s order,
starting at the rate specified in the order.
a. The oxygen liter flow will be adjusted in 1-liter increments in order
to achieve and maintain specific oxygen saturation (Sp02) target
range specified in provider order.
B. Patients will be placed on oxygen to maintain an oxygen saturation
(Sp02) target range.
a. Exception: COPD patients, keep Sp02 between 88-92% (unless otherwise
ordered)
b. Exception: Acute stroke patients, keep Sp02 greater than 94% (unless
otherwise ordered)
C. A nasal cannula is indicated unless unable to maintain the ordered Sp02
target range.
1. Liter flow not to exceed 6 liters/minute (LPM)
2. Assess patient need for continuous pulse oximetry when receiving
greater than or equal to 5 LPM 02 per nasal cannula or Fi02 greater
than 40%
D. If the patient’s Sp02 goal cannot be achieved with the use of a nasal
cannula, the respiratory therapist (RT) should be notified and the RT
may step a patient up to the next oxygen delivery device titrated to the
lowest level of oxygen needed to maintain target Sp02 range. Notify
provider with each device change. If unable to maintain target Sp02,
notify provider immediately for orders. Call Rapid Response if provider
not immediately available.
Simple mask
Venturi mask
OxyMask
Partial/non-rebreathing mask
High flow oxygen
Oe
WRF
MONITORING:
A. Adult patients included in the oxygen therapy protocol will receive
oxygen saturation assessments and titration, if indicated, per
guidelines for modification of oxygen therapy. RT to assess and escalate
therapy as indicated.
B. If patient is in distress, contact physician immediately and do not
leave patient unattended.
C. ABG Indications:
1. If unable to obtain Sp02, a provider should be notified and an ABG
ABG ordered for hemodynamic status.
2. If there are concerns for the patient’s oxygenation or acid-base
status (e.g. increase in confusion/disorientation, diaphoresis, use
of accessory muscles, tachycardia, tachypnea, tachypnea, cyanosis),
a provider should be notified and an ABG ordered.
<End of Protocol>

Category Procedure Name Order Number Date Time Pri Qty Ord Source Status Ordered By
NURORDINP Oxygen Weaning Protocol 20221203-1384 12/03/22 2225 E IPR CHECHO1
Other Provider : xxWILAD Sig Lvl Provider :
Protocol: <Oxygen Weaning Protocol>
-- Oxygen Weaning Protocol: Adult --
MODIFICATION GUIDELINES:
A. Notify patient's nurse of all oxygen titrations if completed by RT.
B. All titrations must be appropriately documented.
C. Once patient is within ordered target Sp02 range and vital signs are
stable per vital sign parameter order, proceed to weaning:
1. Simple face mask patients who require liter flow less than 6 LPM will
need to be switched to a nasal cannula starting with a flow rate of
less than 5 LPM.
2. For patients on blended oxygen, the Fi02 will be managed by RT in
increments of 10% while maintaining the target Sp02 range from order.
3. RT to convert to nasal cannula when Fi02 is less than 402%.
4. Nasal cannula titration will begin with decrease in liter flow by 1
LPM, to lowest liter flow needed to maintain target Sp02 range.
5. If tolerated, continue to wean oxygen to room air, using
discontinuation guidelines.
a. Oxygen therapy should not be discontinued/weaned for patients with
a documented history of chronic hypoxemia (e.g. COPD) that wear
oxygen at home unless otherwise ordered by physician.
D. If patient unable to maintain target Sp02, discontinue weaning and
follow Oxygen Therapy Protocol. Maintain the lowest Fi02/liter flow
required to keep SpO02 at target range.
E. Notify physician if patient is not able to wean for home 02 evaluation
order.
DISCONTINUATION GUIDELINES:
A. Once patient is on 1 LPM or less, place on room air.
1. Check patient’s Sp02 within 1 hour of placing on room air and then
per vital sign order unless otherwise indicated, with proper
documentation.
2. Communicate discontinuation of 02 therapy to appropriate healthcare
professionals.
B. If Sp02 less than ordered target range, resume 02 therapy and follow
Oxygen Therapy Protocol.
<End of Protocol>

Protocol:
Patient: MARSHALL, DEBBIE MRN: G001075275
<MRSA Screen/Targeted Decol.3 Protocol>
MRSA Screening and Targeted Decolonization Protocol
SCREENING:
- Obtain MRSA nares screening swab on ALL admissions for the following
criteria, if none of the listed criteria is met Nursing may cancel the
swab order:
1. Prior MRSA history in Meditech - located within First Point of Contact
screen or Health History
Active MRSA less than 1 year with positive culture and/or active
infection: Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS
History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other
signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS If known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures:
Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS
2. First Point of Contact NUR inpatient admission/transfer queries for
high risk:
Nursing home
Long term care facility
Other healthcare facility
Other hospital
Jail/prison
Homeless shelter
End stage renal dialysis care
Surgical procedure: Open heart, spine, or joint replacement
Known IV Drug User and/or draining wounds
3. Nasal swab should be taken from anterior nares, not deep
-If applicable, primary site (e.g. wound) should also be swabbed
4. Only swab patient's nares who have been off anti-MRSA antibiotics for
at least 48 hours
DECOLONIZATION:
- Targeted decolonization for NON-ICU if MRSA nares screening swab is
POSITIVE, prior history of MRSA within 1 year OR patient is identified
as high risk based on first point of contact screening.
- Universal decolonization for ALL adult and pediatric ICU patients
1. Implement appropriate isolation precautions when MRSA positive for
prior history or current colonization or infection as follows:
Active MRSA less than 1 year with positive culture and/or active
infection : Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS
History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other
signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS If known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures:
Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS
2. Concurrently begin:
Daily chlorhexidine (CHG) bathing for 5 consecutive days or longer if
patient has central venous access device or in ICU
Mupirocin or iodophor to nares twice daily for 5 consecutive days
3. Decolonization criteria:
All patients in Intensive care unit, patients identified as high
risk on the first point of contact screen, patients known to be
MRSA positive by prior history or new positive lab results
Use an alternative for patients with known allergy to mupirocin or
iodine
Continue mupirocin/iodophor nasal product and CHG treatment if
transferred to another level of care to complete 5 full consecutive
days
Apply product to anterior nares for 30 seconds each side (slowly
clockwise for count of 5, counter clockwise for count of 5)
DISCONTINUE CONTACT PRECAUTIONS FOR MRSA:
- After off all anti-MRSA antibiotics and completing the decolonization
protocol for 5 full consecutive days:

Protocol: <Urinary Management Protocol Protocol>
--- URINARY MANAGEMENT PROTOCOL ---
The Urinary Management Protocol is intended to fully empower nursing to
utilize all resources available to them to collect accurate output, with an
initial focus on using non-invasive urinary management methods. If followed
correctly, this should lead to significant reduction in indwelling urinary
catheter (IUC) use.
NOTE: This protocol does not apply to patients who have had urological
surgery, indwelling urinary catheters placed by urology, or have a urology
consult.
PRE-CATHETER AVOIDANCE REVIEW AND EXCLUSION (P-CARE)
On admission, evaluate ability to capture urinary output using the
processes below.
- If IUC is ordered, complete 2-person attestation w/ approval prior to
insertion
* TUCs can be approved up to first 48 hours then reviewed daily for:
Critical 1&0 requiring hourly reads
CBI w/ active hematuria
GU surgery
Proning > 12 hours on paralytics
Sedated AND paralyzed If chronic IUC vetted and ordered, keep in place
Urology ordered: Need active plan of care and oversight while
patient inhouse
- FOR PATIENTS WITH ACUTE RETENTION:
* Perform bladder scan:
“ If residual urine >/= 500 mL:
Drain bladder via in/out catheter
Follow UCARE (see below)
“ If residual urine < 500 mL:
Deploy active voiding (if tolerated):
* Ambulate patient to toilet/BSC
* Stand to void
* Raise HOB, bend knees (urine pose)
* Run hands in warm water
* Gently massage over bladder
* Consider medications (e.g. BPH/alpha blocker)
* Assess/consider other causative factors, such as contributing
meds (e.g. opioids, antihistamines, anticholinergics)
- FOR PATIENTS WITH ACUTE KIDNEY INJURY (AKI) OR END-STAGE RENAL DISEASE
(ESRD) OR KIDNEY DISEASE REQUIRING RENAL REPLACEMENT THERAPY (RRT):
* For patients with ESRD:
“ Discontinue IUC after consulting provider
* For patients with AKI:
“If urinary output >/= 15 mL/hr for > 48 hours:
Discontinue IUC after consulting provider
“If urinary output < 15 mL/hr for > 48 hours:
Perform bladder scan every 6 hours
* Tf residual urine >/= 500 mL:
“Drain bladder via in/out catheter >> >>
> > >
NURSE-DRIVEN FOLEY PROTOCOL (NDFP)
NDFP empowers nursing to remove indwelling urinary catheters (IUC) as soon
as they are no longer clinically indicated. Nurses can remove the urinary
catheter without a specific order or provider approval.
A. Appropriate indications for maintaining an indwelling urinary catheter
include:
1. Accurate 180 and critically i1]
2. Acute retention/obstruction
3. Assist in skin healing

URINARY CATHETER ALGORITHM FOR ACUTE RETENTION AND EARLY REMOVAL (UCARE)
UCARE empowers the nurse to remove the indwelling urinary catheter (IUC)
on day 2 of acute urinary retention and assist patient in using active
voiding measures as listed below. By removing the IUC after the acute time
frame, the current status can be better understood for resolution or
continued issues that may need to be further addressed by specialties.
While in use, nursing can utilize the in/out (straight) catheter with
bladder scan as long as tolerated by the patient.
A. Post IUC removal, follow the Urinary Catheter Algorithm for Acute
Retention and Early Removal (UCARE):
1. Encourage active voiding.
2. If not voided in 4-6 hours, scan bladder.
a. If < 180 mL: Assess intake, encourage active voiding, reassess in
4 hours.
b. If 180-500 mL: Encourage active voiding. If not voiding within 2
hours, scan bladder.
1. If residual urine < 180 mL: No further action, continue to
monitor.
2. Residual urine > 180 mL: Continue active voiding, report
residual volume to primary team.
3. NO residual urine: Repeat algorithm
c. If > 500 mL: Perform in/out catheter and repeat algorithm
1. May perform in/out catheter for a minimum of 4 cycles and
continue as tolerated
3. If voiding spontaneously: continue to monitor
<End of Protocol>

Protocol: <Telemetry Removal NDP Protocol>
-- Telemetry Nurse Driven Removal Protocol --
Telemetry with nurse driven removal protocol - telemetry can be
discontinued without an additional MD order if patient no longer meets
criteria for protocol.
TELEMETRY MONITORING INDICATED:
1. Significant arrhythmia requiring medical therapy: SVT (supraventricular
tachycardia), bradycardia, A. Fib (atrial fibrillation) with RVR (rapid
ventricular response)
2. Acute coronary syndrome or unstable angina with NSTEMI (non-ST elevation
myocardial infarction) or STEMI (ST-elevation myocardial infarction)
3. Pre or post PCI (percutaneous cardiac intervention), CABG (coronary
artery bypass with graft), EP (electrophysiology) study, pacemaker or
AICD (automatic internal cardiac defibrillator) implantation
4. Medical/surgical patients on IV beta blockers, IV digoxin, ionotropic
drips, or other medications requiring close cardiac monitoring (does not
include obstetrical patients)
5. Moderate to severe hypokalemia (less than or equal to 3.0) or severe
hypomagnesemia (less than or equal to 1.3)
6. Drug or chemical toxicity
7. Suspected pacemaker or AICD malfunction
8. Resuscitated from cardiac arrest or unstable VT (ventricular
tachycardia)
9. Syncope of unknown etiology
10. Stroke patients
11. Post vascular procedure
12. Acute decompensated heart failure
13. Sepsis
TELEMETRY NOT INDICATED FOR:
1. Patients who are stable and arrhythmia free for 48 hours of consecutive
monitoring and does not meet any criteria in the ‘Telemetry Monitoring
Indicated’ list
2. Terminally il] and not a candidate for therapy for arrhythmia
medications, comfort care patients
3. Patients with chronic, rate controlled, stable A. Fib
4. Patients with asymptomatic PVCs (premature ventricular contractions) not
hospitalized for cardiac reasons
<End of Protocol>
